## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / nonlinear oscillators
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration (dv/dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of position x, velocity v, and time t. The acceleration arises from combinations of nonlinear restoring forces, nonlinear damping, and possibly periodic driving forces.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (Duffing with linear damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodic driving force)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (c2 - x**2) (nonlinear damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing with drive)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Damped pendulum: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (sinusoidal restoring + damping)
- Quintic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order nonlinear restoring)
- Quadratic-cubic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric nonlinearity)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (Rayleigh-type nonlinear damping)
- Position-velocity coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (mixed nonlinearity)
- Driven damped pendulum: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear pendulum)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium — characteristic of symmetric potential wells
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v represent energy dissipation (damping) or injection; sign determines if energy is added or removed
- Products of position powers and velocity (e.g., x**2 * v) indicate amplitude-dependent damping, hallmark of Van der Pol type self-excited oscillations
- Sinusoidal functions of position sin(c*x) indicate a periodic potential landscape, as in pendulum dynamics
- Explicit sinusoidal time dependence cos(c*t) or sin(c*t) signals external periodic forcing/driving
- Cubic position terms x**3 with sign opposite to linear term x indicate a double-well (bistable) Duffing potential
- Cubic position terms x**3 with same sign as linear term x indicate a hardening/softening spring nonlinearity
- Even-power position terms (x**2) break the spatial symmetry and indicate asymmetric restoring forces
